    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

<span id="freeTextContainer2221958497042338954">The Present is the second book in the VanWest series. <br/><br/>To defeat the Universal Council, VanWest is made to confront his dark past. Uncovering Mars’s many secrets and the coming together of Earth’s main opposition groups could prove pivotal in defeating the Council’s mighty Space Army. However, success is not what it appears, for there’s a twist that he could not foresee.</span>

<div id="review_3488469369" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3488469369" />
    <a title="The one with all the plants and books!" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/119525664-the-one-with-all-the-plants-and-books"><img alt="The one with all the plants and books!" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3488469369?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The one with all the plants and books!" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The one with all the plants and books!" href="/user/show/119525664-the-one-with-all-the-plants-and-books">The one with all the plants and books!</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3488469369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14593234477846529355">I always approach second and subsequent novels in a series with apprehension. Nowhere was this more so than with the second in the VanWest series, The Present.<br/>Having read and thoroughly enjoyed the first book, The Past, it was apparent that the next installment had much to live up to. Also, I loved the character of VanWest and hated the thought of this time, not being able to gell entirely with him.<br/>I needn’t have worried – for VanWest The Present takes up immediately where The Past leaves off. B</span>
  <span id="freeText14593234477846529355" style="display:none">I always approach second and subsequent novels in a series with apprehension. Nowhere was this more so than with the second in the VanWest series, The Present.<br />Having read and thoroughly enjoyed the first book, The Past, it was apparent that the next installment had much to live up to. Also, I loved the character of VanWest and hated the thought of this time, not being able to gell entirely with him.<br />I needn’t have worried – for VanWest The Present takes up immediately where The Past leaves off. Better still, Kenneth continues to work his literary magic!<br />After a short and snappy prologue, which is enough to throw you straight back into the story, the pace is instantly picked up as VanWest works his way to Mars. Yet along the way, as we’ve come to expect, his mission doesn’t run smoothly, and many other strands begin to unravel. This makes for perhaps a more fulfilling experience than the first book, in my personal opinion.<br />Perhaps the best example of this is in the chapter titled A Trip Down Memory Lane. As I’m not a huge sci-fi fan and only occasionally read this genre, it’s often hard to keep up and understand these types of books. Sci-fi books I’ve found are often more immense when it comes to characters, places, and indeed several periods.<br />But, I have never once felt left behind when reading VanWest, and this second book was no different. That’s not to say that Thomas changes his writing, rather, his descriptive prose evokes more of the imagination, and I find myself more than capable of keeping up.<br />Chapter 17 is a perfect example of how the book works hard on the senses. Perhaps one of the most atmospheric of sections, it’s a literary haven of death, confusion, an unknown energy and a massive dose of reality for VanWest. It’s also a fantastic nod to VanWest’s visions/senses. <br />The Present is also a book that manages to flesh out more of VanWest’s character. This is something those fans of his from book one will certainly enjoy, especially as here we witness the relationship building between him and Iris.<br />As for the ending, Kenneth isn’t ready just yet to offer VanWest his HEA, and once again, the scene is set for book 3! Still, if he can keep up the pace created in books one and two, the third VanWest book should be one heck of a ride!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14593234477846529355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3573417268" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3573417268" />
    <a title="Slmarie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51360613-slmarie"><img alt="Slmarie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452464271p2/51360613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3573417268?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Slmarie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Slmarie" href="/user/show/51360613-slmarie">Slmarie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3573417268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17792715159521337401">The second book in VanWest series, VanWest: The Present, begins with a thorough prologue that offers new readers a robust introduction to the adventures partaken by protagonist VanWest in the first book of the series, VanWest: The Past. Although I highly recommend starting with the first VanWest book, this second book is skillfully written and may work well as a stand-alone novel. The author, Kenneth Thomas, has a beautiful descriptive writing style for ushering readers forward throughout the ac</span>
  <span id="freeText17792715159521337401" style="display:none">The second book in VanWest series, VanWest: The Present, begins with a thorough prologue that offers new readers a robust introduction to the adventures partaken by protagonist VanWest in the first book of the series, VanWest: The Past. Although I highly recommend starting with the first VanWest book, this second book is skillfully written and may work well as a stand-alone novel. The author, Kenneth Thomas, has a beautiful descriptive writing style for ushering readers forward throughout the action of the story, bringing the words of an imaginative and thrilling space-travel plot to life. Methodologically written, Thomas extrapolates the series upon current events from our actual Earthly timeline in order to further emphasize the dystopian nightmare the citizens of Earth are up against and what VanWest will do in his present to correct the evolution of humanity. Set in a dystopian future on Earth during the year 3000, VanWest: The Present is brimming with intrigue as various character plots and motives intertwine during an uprising for a global power-grab with the fate of humanity on the line. Joining forces with the Utopians in order to secure humanity’s future, VanWest is reunited with his long-lost childhood friend Iris who is the daughter of the Utopian leader. Together, whilst meeting new characters along the way, they set out to stop the Universal Council Elites from regaining control over the now uprising populous. Just as captivating as VanWest and his strengthening psychic abilities is the development of minor characters in the plot. With the fight for humanity’s “New Beginning” sprung forth, readers engross in a teacher-student face-off for unprecedented democracy, a cyborg invasion for imposing martial law, ruthless warlords negotiating to band together, and decisions to trust outer-space smugglers operating solely for the love of “moolah.” Each chapter in this novel is charged with vibrant and enthralling adventures as readers get to enjoy creative and amusing scenes flourishing in futuristic Sci-Fi flair. Clever, magical, entertaining, and occasionally humorous, VanWest: The Present delivers a compounded and augmented plot, arguably surmounting its prequel. Thoroughly enjoyed, I highly recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17792715159521337401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3513110064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3513110064" />
    <a title="Meg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9401305-meg"><img alt="Meg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544220728p2/9401305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3513110064?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meg" href="/user/show/9401305-meg">Meg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3513110064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13151538641639789673">I enjoyed reading Kenneth Thomas' scifi adventure novel VanWest: The Past, so I was excited to read the sequel, VanWest: The Present.<br/><br/>The beginning of this novel reminds readers where they are in this dark future world.  VanWest begins in the underworld of New Jersey, ready to make the shady, dangerous deal that will get him to Mars to continue his quest. Readers will see some old friends, as well as a wild variety of new characters in this almost cyberpunk adventure. VanWest is still our hero, a</span>
  <span id="freeText13151538641639789673" style="display:none">I enjoyed reading Kenneth Thomas' scifi adventure novel VanWest: The Past, so I was excited to read the sequel, VanWest: The Present.<br /><br />The beginning of this novel reminds readers where they are in this dark future world.  VanWest begins in the underworld of New Jersey, ready to make the shady, dangerous deal that will get him to Mars to continue his quest. Readers will see some old friends, as well as a wild variety of new characters in this almost cyberpunk adventure. VanWest is still our hero, and readers will see him tested again. <br /><br />The writing style in VanWest: The Present is a lot like the first book, blending the simple, declarative narration describing a complex scifi universe, with lots of moving pieces, and stylized dialogue to show characters' backgrounds and personalities.  And the worldbuilding still works, the factions have believable goals in this future, and the twists work well in the established world. <br /><br />Although the factions of this universe are creative science fiction inventions, there's the same familiarity with current social issues that worked so well in the first VanWest novel. The concerns of inequality are present through this novel,  while the story offers scifi conflict between the fictional Universal Council and the Earth Resistance.  There's also an uplifting theme of allies and friendship that really works in a dystopian future. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13151538641639789673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jake O&#39;callaghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jake O&#39;callaghan" href="/user/show/16176091-jake-o-callaghan">Jake O&#39;callaghan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3515600495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15419616227833057306">There aren't many up and coming writers that I follow closely, but Kenneth Thomas is worth watching.<br/>The Present is his 2nd book in the VanWest series. I had it preordered but only recently found the time to read it and man am I glad I did. <br/><br/>I loved the past but actually enjoy the 2nd book more. Since we are already aware of the vibrant world, we can go straight to the action. It's like in Star Wars. The New Hope was incredible but The Emperor Strikes Back is even better because it has a powerful </span>
  <span id="freeText15419616227833057306" style="display:none">There aren't many up and coming writers that I follow closely, but Kenneth Thomas is worth watching.<br />The Present is his 2nd book in the VanWest series. I had it preordered but only recently found the time to read it and man am I glad I did. <br /><br />I loved the past but actually enjoy the 2nd book more. Since we are already aware of the vibrant world, we can go straight to the action. It's like in Star Wars. The New Hope was incredible but The Emperor Strikes Back is even better because it has a powerful base. This sentiment applies these first two books in the series.<br /><br />My favorite part is the way the characters interact with each other. They feel fully 3-dimensional and a part of this fantasy world. This isn't a book where you will find yourself immersed in the world but zoning out a big when the characters talk - the people here really say things that are memorable and attention-grabbing.<br /><br />This series continues to subvert expectations. Just when you think you know what's going on, the author throws a curveball. And, the "curveball" doesn't feel cheap but rather a realistic part of the world. He really kept me engaged throughout the whole novel. Great pacing.<br /><br />Kenneth Thomas continues to explore the interesting themes from The Past. Though I finished this fast-paced book quickly, I thought about the concepts covered for days after. Yes, this book is entertaining but it has substance too. <br /><br />This is a truly thrilling middle chapter to this trilogy. I was a little hesitant coming in as middle books are notorious for having filler, but, in many ways, this is even better than the Past. It has definitely kept me engaged and wanting more so I can't wait until The Future is released.<br /><br />If you're a sci-fi fan, I encourage you to give this book (and series in general) a shot. And, if you only dip your toes into the genre, I promise you won't be disappointed. This is definitely an incredible read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15419616227833057306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16547603062730397907" style="display:none">I was excited to read the book as I've read and enjoyed VanWest The Past. <br />I'm always worried about sequels being disappointing or just being a bridge for book 3. I'm happy to say that it was not the case with The Present. <br />It was as gripping as book 1 and the writing was even better. It is always good to support indie authors with great books like this. <br />VanWest's adventures continues in this book. Somethings are familiar while we get introduced to newer things in the universe. A good post apocalyptic world story always acts as a cautionary tale. It parallels with today's world and imagines what would happen if we took an ideology too far. This book does it well and I'm curious where the author will take it next.</span>

<div id="review_3522985691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3522985691" />
    <a title="Julie Porter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75883518-julie-porter"><img alt="Julie Porter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514904632p2/75883518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3522985691?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Porter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Porter" href="/user/show/75883518-julie-porter">Julie Porter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/54775406-the-present">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3522985691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16833174760690719719"><br/><br/>Spoilers: Previously on VanWest: The Past, VanWest, the ultimate super soldier and Universal Games champion, traveled back in time to stop a resistance group called The Utopians from changing the past by halting Earth's environmental destruction and the Universal Council's stranglehold on the 30th century. <br/>After VanWest infiltrated the Utopians, he was drawn by their philosophies and became enamored with his former childhood friend, Iris VonHelmann, daughter of the Utopian leader Prof. VonHelman</span>
  <span id="freeText16833174760690719719" style="display:none"><br /><br />Spoilers: Previously on VanWest: The Past, VanWest, the ultimate super soldier and Universal Games champion, traveled back in time to stop a resistance group called The Utopians from changing the past by halting Earth's environmental destruction and the Universal Council's stranglehold on the 30th century. <br />After VanWest infiltrated the Utopians, he was drawn by their philosophies and became enamored with his former childhood friend, Iris VonHelmann, daughter of the Utopian leader Prof. VonHelman, AKA "Mad Newton". He also learned that he was the clone of the last Martian President and his psychic abilities foretold that his former allies will slaughter his new ones. <br />VanWest,once the pride of the Universal Council Elite Enforcers, joined the Utopians and became involved in their attempt to assasinate the ruthless UC leader, Dr. King. The assasination attempt and trip to the past ended badly. However, the Utopians made new allies with Van West's former squadron, the Enforcers.<br /> Now, Iris, VanWest, and computer hacker, LeSouris are in New Jersey's underground trying to obtain a ship to Mars while VonHelman seeks to recruit new allies to join the resistance against the Universal Council.<br /><br />Kenneth Thomas's VanWest The Present is a teriffic follow up to the previous book, The Past. It is not as complex as the previous volume with the various scenes of time travel and double crosses that further confuses the plot. The Present's plot is pretty straightforward, separating into mostly two distinct storylines and emerges the better for it. Besides the major settings between two very intriguing locations of Mars and the Underground Cities in New Jersey are well-written and described.<br /><br />A group of New Jerseyans settled in the abandoned tunnels in the Garden State, forming their own underground societies in which the cities are connected via an intricate network. Because they have been underground for so long, the New Jerseyans have evolved to adapt to their surroundings, such as enhanced eyesight, resistance to radiation, and gills. They also have unusual speech patterns such as removing some verbs such as "am," "is", and "are." ("Them two on news wire all the time! This brings heat to my casino!")<br />New Jersey's income largely depends on the literal underworld. It is filled with underground casinos and Papini traders. (Papini is an addictive drug that promises relief from radiation poisoning). The underground underworld is led by several warlords, one of whom is Method A.<br /><br />Method A is a flamboyant character that calls to mind Aunty Entity, Tina Turner's character in Mad Max Beyond The Thunderdome. She shamelessly flaunts her wealth from gambling and narcotics, but rules her people with firmness and protectiveness. When VanWest, Iris, and LeSouris arrive in Jersey to try to get a transport to Mars, Method A is naturally concerned that their presence will bring Super Soldiers to her tunnels. However, the promise of moolah (money) and VanWest's prescient warning of their arrival changes her mind. Once an antihero looking out for Number One, Method A becomes a card carrying member of the Resistance and this Reader's favorite character in the series.<br />The nice thing that Thomas does in this book is expand the POV from VanWest and Iris to other characters. Method A in particular benefits from this. While VanWest, Iris, and La Souris are in Mars, Readers return to Method A's doings as she and her people fight the Super Soldiers and broker alliances with other warlords with clever names like Rulez Haah and Gangs Hater. During the Universal Council's attack on Jersey's underground, Method A shows true leadership abilities as she guides her people to safety while fighting the soldiers and negotiating with the other warlords. <br /><br />Meanwhile VanWest's exploration of his past on Mars is moving and heartfelt. This journey has a great setting for him to explore it. Mars proves to be a contrast to the dying Earth. Instead the Red Planet is brimming with life and beauty. <br />There is a volcanic plain which spews eye-catching vivid red and yellow plumes of lava. Ornate murals that reveal Martian history surround a chamber. The "Face on Mars" mountain makes an appearance and still seems to form a human face (and has become a tourist attraction). There are many spaceports filled with wide varieties of visitors from miners to drug dealers.<br /><br /> The more VanWest, Iris, and LaSouris travel through this alien landscape, the more VanWest gets flashes of the life of Dederic Vander Westhuizen, the last Martian President and the man from whom VanWest was cloned. He sees his wife and family. He sees his battles and arguments with the Universal Council. VanWest is haunted by the ghost of Vander Westhuizen's daughter who points him in the right direction to learn about his own history and that of his predecessor.<br />VanWest also recalls his life and early training as a clone forced to follow the UC's lead and given no other options in life. An eerie passage occurs when VanWest finds himself inside a lab and comes face to face with other clones of Vander Westhuizen. They are similar to VanWest in appearance, characteristics, and abilities including psychic abilities. VanWest is able to use that to his advantage as he mentally communicates with his fellow clones so they can fight the Council and the soldiers.<br /><br />The final chapters feature extensive battles in Mars and Jersey. These chapters shine with action, suspense, and betrayal. Alliances are formed and some are permanently broken. People question the motives of an important character who has been around since the previous book to the point that it is possible that the character may emerge as an antagonist in the next volume.<br /> The final pages reveal promise for a better future, one of cooperation and community over conquest and violence. However, there might be trouble on the horizon, trouble that will no doubt be the focus of the next volume, VanWest: The Future.<br /><br />If The Future is anything like the previous volumes of The Past and Present, it should be a bright future indeed.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16833174760690719719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59585817-sara-corpuz?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59585817-sara-corpuz?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3554363166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2827188311804227545">DISCLAIMER: I was lucky enough to read this book after the author reached out to me. I hope the prospective reader will read this review fully before making any prejudgments on the book. I will give the book my thoughts, good and bad. Also, this review contains opinions that are my own and not the author’s. My thoughts will be different from your thoughts and just know that before reading the book. <br/><br/>After reading the first book in the VanWest series, The Past, I read on to The Present. This takes</span>
  <span id="freeText2827188311804227545" style="display:none">DISCLAIMER: I was lucky enough to read this book after the author reached out to me. I hope the prospective reader will read this review fully before making any prejudgments on the book. I will give the book my thoughts, good and bad. Also, this review contains opinions that are my own and not the author’s. My thoughts will be different from your thoughts and just know that before reading the book. <br><br>After reading the first book in the VanWest series, The Past, I read on to The Present. This takes place after the first novel. VanWest has to confront his dark past. This is what has to be done to defeat the universal council. To defeat the Council’s space army, he has to uncover the many secrets of Mars and bring together Earth’s main opposition groups. VanWest sees success, but nothing is what it seems. There is a twist of fate that he could never have foreseen.<br><br>I love that there was a reminder of the world that we were living in. VanWest is experiencing a dark world that he thinks is the end. I love the addition of the universe that we know in this book. It is exhilarating to be able to have what we know as Mars in the story. The first and second book have the same style in writing. It made for the perfect continuality that was easy to connect the points that were important in the first book and the second. If you think of the book as a thread and you connect the first and second, you find that it threads in and out of the books. They are connected almost at a deeper level.<br><br>The characters in this book are just as amazing as the first! I want to talk about the most important thing that can ruin a second story is when the characters seem different in the second book than the first. There is something that is amazing about a book that has the same people and they act the same way. I felt as if I could read the first and second book mixed, and the people would all have the same personality. This is an amazing feat. I wasn’t expecting this kind of brilliance from an up and coming author.<br><br>My Rating: This is absolutely a 5 out of 5 stars. Since the first book was fast paced in setting, the second needed to be as well. This was fast paced all in the right ways. I think it is a book and an author worth watching. This book is a read again, as well as the first one. This was such a different book for me to read. I am not regretting it at all. I am so glad I took a chance on a new story. I would recommend this book to the readers who don’t read sci-fi, don’t read a lot, or the readers who want to take a chance on a brand-new adventure that is truly out of this world. <br><br>I hope this review helps you in making your next book choice. Happy reading!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/20310792.Kenneth_Thomas" title="Kenneth Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">Kenneth Thomas</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54775299.The_Present__VanWest___2_" title="The Present (VanWest, #2) by Kenneth Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1596279356l/54775299._SY75_.jpg" alt="The Present (VanWest, #2) by Kenneth Thomas" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_3586611511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3586611511" />
    <a title="Anne Mellar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/122422603-anne-mellar"><img alt="Anne Mellar" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3586611511?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne Mellar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne Mellar" href="/user/show/122422603-anne-mellar">Anne Mellar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3586611511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9557194845711898189"><i>The Present</i> follows immediately on from where <i>The Past</i>, the first book in Kenneth Thomas’s sci-fi series, left off, plunging you straight back into the heart of the action. Troubled by the conflict between humanity, technology and machinery, the solar system is teetering on the edge of full-blown war.<br/><br/>Dodging the dreaded sequel blues, this feels very much like a step-up in gear and scope from the first book, which was more of a personal odyssey for protagonist VanWest. In <i>The Present</i>, the fightba</span>
  <span id="freeText9557194845711898189" style="display:none"><i>The Present</i> follows immediately on from where <i>The Past</i>, the first book in Kenneth Thomas’s sci-fi series, left off, plunging you straight back into the heart of the action. Troubled by the conflict between humanity, technology and machinery, the solar system is teetering on the edge of full-blown war.<br /><br />Dodging the dreaded sequel blues, this feels very much like a step-up in gear and scope from the first book, which was more of a personal odyssey for protagonist VanWest. In <i>The Present</i>, the fightback against the Universal Council’s oppressive regime and their bionic Space Army begins in earnest. The story takes a step back to deliver a much more panoramic telling of events as they unfold on a galactic scale.<br /><br />Here we see the military strategizing and manoeuvring of different antagonists – Free Enforcers, Jerseyans, Martians and Utopians – as they square up to the unbeatable cyborg army. In this David versus Goliath battle for the fate of the universe, it’s now crunch time. Caught in the midst of it all, VanWest is propelled on a personal mission to assassinate the Universal Council’s leader and uncover the truth of his own story of origin. <br /><br />Just as with the first book, Thomas’s writing skilfully immerses us into this well-fleshed out world. The narrator’s voice holds back from overpowering the story, but delivers it in the dispassionate tones of a observer. This controlled scripting allows the action to move at a breakneck pace as the narrative choreographs a series of high-definition warring skirmishes. <br /> <br />Ultimately, <i>The Present</i> resonates with very modern ideas about green energy technology, colonisation, scientific experimentation and our own Covid-19’s era dependency on technology. It comes as no surprise, then, that this rollercoaster narrative ends, in typical fashion, on a cliff-hanger that’ll have you looking towards… <i>The Future</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9557194845711898189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7647394604233124749" style="display:none">What an amazing adventure!<br /><br />The VanWest series continue to surprise me.<br /> Just when I thought I couldn't like these books more... it happened. <br /><br />Action-packed ☑️<br />New perspectives and characters ☑️<br />A whole new language and cultural diversity ☑️<br />Good vs Evil battles ☑️<br />Exciting plot twists ☑️<br /><br />The whole book kept me turning pages surprisingly fast. Each of them acted according to their personal beliefs and some of them even died for them.<br />And well... that ending! It was all good and then -- a final Plot-Twist! <br />I don't even know how am I supposed to wait until 2023 for Book #3 to come out. <br /><br />VanWest The Present is for sure one of those books you won't be able to get out of your head once you have read it, as well as VanWest The Past. <span id="freeTextContainer2791768781191823121">I literally couldn't wait to read this after finishing the first book yesterday. This picks up right after the first book ends, so don't worry.<br/>Although its pace is fast, this story never leaves you behind. The twists are believable and the protagonist is tested again, all while the world continues to be built with enjoyable dialogue and solid characters delivered in a clean, simple narrative. <br/><br/>While continuing its commentary on climate change and other societal, worldly issues, you will find your</span>
  <span id="freeText2791768781191823121" style="display:none">I literally couldn't wait to read this after finishing the first book yesterday. This picks up right after the first book ends, so don't worry.<br />Although its pace is fast, this story never leaves you behind. The twists are believable and the protagonist is tested again, all while the world continues to be built with enjoyable dialogue and solid characters delivered in a clean, simple narrative. <br /><br />While continuing its commentary on climate change and other societal, worldly issues, you will find yourself continuously asking "now what? And then what?" at every turn. Not in an annoying way either! Kenneth really continued his first book in an intensely satisfying way, in which the characters you already like continue to solidify themselves as your friends or people you enjoy disliking, while pushing you to continue on the self-reflection from the first book.<br /><br />Though there is a brief recap for you if you start with this book, I really do not recommend you ignore the first book. It's a trilogy for a reason. This story has a rich diegesis and requires you to immerse yourself in it. There's a lot you're missing out on if you don't!<br /><br />Sequels are often done poorly; this is not one of those times. I highly recommend this series. I look forward to the third book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2791768781191823121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText3194144128062630120" style="display:none">The second installment of the VanWest series not only ties in perfectly with the first, but shows Kenneth Thomas' writing to be as engaging as ever. <br /><br />Having got into the first one very much, I ended up reading them both over two days. This book more than satiated my hunger to remain in Thomas' world. Almost filmic in its speed and heavy reliance on action sequences, The Present portrays Captain VanWest as demanding and alluring a protagonist as ever.<br /><br />The faintly hidden allusions to our own current climate crisis suited me well too. I always like to relate to something in a novel and typically do not find this easy to do with time travel things. Forming his dystopia from the current world around him, however, Kenneth Thomas presents something in this book that I was able to relate to. <br /><br />I'm excited for the third instalment that is scheduled for release on 2023! Not sure I can wait that long...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8385595676958115377">The second in Kenneth Thomas' dystopian trilogy.<br/><br/>You will find yourself purchasing this the moment you finish the first in the series. <br/>The book has an incredible twist of plot which will come completely unexpected. 'The Present' has more of those scenarios that inevitably leave us questioning our own lives, which is one thing I love about these books! Another must read!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3585202207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3585202207" />
    <a title="Olivia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62914750-olivia"><img alt="Olivia" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3585202207?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia" href="/user/show/62914750-olivia">Olivia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3585202207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17490877201747096444">For anyone who’s drawn to the darkness within literature — the emotional, the hypothetical, the ethical — this book is for them. I enjoyed the first VanWest book, but this is definitely my favorite of the two. Kenneth’s rich imagination and endless supply of lore continues as VanWest seeks to liberate the galaxy from its oppressive rulers, The Universal Council. The universe created by Kenneth is bursting with accents from every theme and genre one could imagine. In some parts of the novels, I t</span>
  <span id="freeText17490877201747096444" style="display:none">For anyone who’s drawn to the darkness within literature — the emotional, the hypothetical, the ethical — this book is for them. I enjoyed the first VanWest book, but this is definitely my favorite of the two. Kenneth’s rich imagination and endless supply of lore continues as VanWest seeks to liberate the galaxy from its oppressive rulers, The Universal Council. The universe created by Kenneth is bursting with accents from every theme and genre one could imagine. In some parts of the novels, I think of Star Wars. In others, the Hunger Games. In more, 1984. What makes these books unique, however, is the culmination of all these things which have been fused together to form a story I truly have never come across before.<br /><br />Its thematic elements are solid. Stylistically, the book in entirety is striking in its contrast. For me, this means VanWest: The Present is impressive in that it is peppered with the softest imagery amidst a story that is quite literally about war, eugenics, AI, and totalitarianism. <br /><br />I can see the sky when the narrator describes the clouds as “grey and acidic”, and I can feel the climate illuminated as “sweet and warm.” The ability to soften a war-scarred novel with imagery that invokes tender, more delicate sensations is indicative of a writer who’s well-rounded and can support their story with sensory details that humanize the experience for their readers. I look for that in the literature I read and Kenneth straight up delivered. Also — a bonus point for the Emily Dickinson poetry. After all, what is a futuristic fantasy without callbacks to the past?<br /><br />As for the story itself, I admire Kenneth’s ability to manipulate the characters fearlessly, and with purpose. While I’m a sucker for a good pairing (looking at you VanWest and Iris) I love a tragic backstory even more. VanWest’s past is truly a history of pain and deceit. When he learns the truth of who he is and what he was originally destined for, I felt the heart of the series be revealed. I’d invite Kenneth to really dive deep into that abyss. Readers want to find themselves in the pages of a book and with all of the high, sci-fi/historical lore, I think there’s an insane amount of potential in the character’s backstories alone. That’s where the humanity is.<br /><br />Overall, an exciting read. I’d recommend reading the first book before ‘The Present’ because of the many terms/references drawn upon from its predecessor. The first book is also vital when understanding VanWest’s evolution from soldier to liberator. I really had fun with ‘The Present’ and do recommend it for those who enjoy novels with futuristic / sci-fi / historical fiction / dystopian themes!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17490877201747096444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3621433605" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3621433605" />
    <a title="Teresa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8064843-teresa"><img alt="Teresa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330980885p2/8064843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3621433605?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teresa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teresa" href="/user/show/8064843-teresa">Teresa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3621433605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16089489740914467846">Kenneth Thomas is at it again with another exciting VanWest adventure. Following the events of The Past, VanWest and his friends investigate mysterious clues leading them to Mars. The conspiracy comes to light as VanWest learns more about his past and Mars’ lost history.<br/><br/>The Present expands Thomas’s world. The first novel in the series was focused, centering on VanWest and the politics in Antarctica. Now, we explore new places through the perspective of different characters. From the gang-like po</span>
  <span id="freeText16089489740914467846" style="display:none">Kenneth Thomas is at it again with another exciting VanWest adventure. Following the events of The Past, VanWest and his friends investigate mysterious clues leading them to Mars. The conspiracy comes to light as VanWest learns more about his past and Mars’ lost history.<br /><br />The Present expands Thomas’s world. The first novel in the series was focused, centering on VanWest and the politics in Antarctica. Now, we explore new places through the perspective of different characters. From the gang-like power struggles of New Jersey to the politics of Earth’s capital of Queen Elizabeth in Antarctica and the red sands of Mars. The Past was filled with secret battles and one-on-one confrontations. The Present explodes onto the scene with cinematic space battles and large-scale invasions. The stakes and scope of the story increased. It’s gratifying to watch the characters struggle and rise to their challenges.<br /><br />Thomas has a knack for weaving many different elements into his stories. We encounter symbolism from Emily Dickenson poetry, American surfer culture and ancient mythology. By combining these with classic science fiction tropes, Thomas creates a unique and captivating tale. Readers with an understanding of these components read deeper into the novel, drawing on inferences to gain a deeper understanding of the greater lore of Earth 3000.<br /><br />The VanWest books are fun adventure-dystopian stories. A roller coaster of action, intrigue and romance, they are perfect to curl up with on a rainy day. I’m excited for the further adventures of Captain VanWest. Keep an eye out for the third book in 2023.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16089489740914467846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3524229889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18280348648026558676">Having been left with a desire for more after reading the first book of this series, I couldn't resist but reading its sequel straight away. <br/><br/>In the Present, our old friend Captain VanWest must confront his dark past if he wants to defeat the authoritarian Universal Council he works for. This is the reason that leads him to travel to Mars (making a stopover in New Jersey) which he reaches in turn not without encountering a number of obstacles on his way there. <br/><br/>The whole plot gets more and more en</span>
  <span id="freeText18280348648026558676" style="display:none">Having been left with a desire for more after reading the first book of this series, I couldn't resist but reading its sequel straight away. <br /><br />In the Present, our old friend Captain VanWest must confront his dark past if he wants to defeat the authoritarian Universal Council he works for. This is the reason that leads him to travel to Mars (making a stopover in New Jersey) which he reaches in turn not without encountering a number of obstacles on his way there. <br /><br />The whole plot gets more and more entangled over time. There is a lot of alliances building through character interaction taking place during this fast-paced masterfully narrated trip to a land whose inhabitants have long disappeared. <br /><br />In this middle chapter, Captain VanWest will have to face the truth of his origin by getting in contact with someone from his past who owns the key to his existence. A tough but necessary step in the storyline.<br /><br />Another futuristic masterpiece set in the year 3000 that any Sci-Fi lover should not miss. If you haven't read the first chapter yet, my recommendation is that you do so before immersing yourself in this new instalment of the futuristic dystopia of the VanWest series. <br /><br />I was excited to see the new chapter of what has become one of my favourite reads. Like the time before I did not stop reading until the book was over so caught up I was with the plot along with the further development of VanWest. <br /><br />Hoping that the next instalment doesn't take to long to come out since really need to know what happens next asap!<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText35029039872595895" style="display:none">I had read and thoroughly enjoyed the first book in the Vanwest trilogy, titled Vanwest:The Past. <br />Ever since, I've been anticipating the release of the second book to learn about how the story progressed.   <span id="freeText16055087158071887576" style="display:none">Read this book in one go after falling in love with #1 in the series. Surprisingly, it's better than the first one! We already know the world, so we can jump straight into the action. <br />It's a gripping action-thriller, dystopian plot, with new characters that feel 3-dimensional and a part of the fantasy world we know. You listen to what they say. Plus, the amazing world-building complements them and drives you into the story. That and, with the social themes still there, you're purely engaged and wanting more. It's an entertaining book with more substance than you'd think. Not sure I can wait until #3 is out. <br />If you're a sci-fi fan, I encourage you to give this series a shot. And even if you're just starting in the genre, you won't be disappointed. This is a brilliant middle chapter to the trilogy. <br /><br />Highly recommend the series and author!!</span>

  <span id="freeText8441217305187548115" style="display:none">The second book in the VanWest trilogy certainly doesn’t disappoint. Like its predecessor The Past, the second entry, The Present, continues to mirror and explores issues in our own world, including social inequalities and lockdowns. <br /><br />As always, Kenneth Thomas unveils a detailed universe with lots to discover, revealing many worlds that each hold their own secrets. Readers won’t be bored with this book, as it comes packed with its own ups and downs, twists and turns. <br /><br />Importantly, this second part of the VanWest trilogy considers resistance. This seems particularly prescient in our contemporary world, and is surely a necessary step for humans living in late 21st century capitalism. <br /><br />Science fiction is always important, and it continues to be so!<br /><br /><br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3478183734" />
    <a title="Keith Wilson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/115614896-keith-wilson"><img alt="Keith Wilson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590753638p2/115614896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115614896-keith-wilson?shelf=dystopian-thriller">dystopian-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115614896-keith-wilson?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115614896-keith-wilson?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115614896-keith-wilson?shelf=action">action</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3478183734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4312106466170458976">The Past (#1) was very innovative and refreshingly original, combining dystopia, historical fiction and time-travel as it moved seamlessly through the futuristic setting of the year 3000 (in the Universal Games) to 1950s Paris and 1990s Florida as the Enforcer Captain VanWest tracked down a renegade sect bent on stopping technological and scientific progress in the late 20th Century.<br/><br/>The Present (#2), British author Kenneth Thomas delivers another fast-paced masterpiece. VanWest having decided be</span>
  <span id="freeText4312106466170458976" style="display:none">The Past (#1) was very innovative and refreshingly original, combining dystopia, historical fiction and time-travel as it moved seamlessly through the futuristic setting of the year 3000 (in the Universal Games) to 1950s Paris and 1990s Florida as the Enforcer Captain VanWest tracked down a renegade sect bent on stopping technological and scientific progress in the late 20th Century.<br /><br />The Present (#2), British author Kenneth Thomas delivers another fast-paced masterpiece. VanWest having decided between his masters (the Universal Council) and the newly formed EaR (Earth's Resistance, which includes the NEA and Utopians) he heads to New Jersey and then Mars. I really enjoyed exploring the Jerseyan world (those living underground on Earth) as well as the mystery and intrigue in discovering more about the (now extinct) Martians and his origins.<br /><br />VanWest's mission to Mars converges with other story-lines involving the Jerseyans, the NEA-Utopians, the Enforcers (there is a lot of plotting and ally building). The book felt very current, covering topics such as lock-downs, redundancies, inequalities. Method A proved to be a very cool and interesting character - with her own style, customs and way of speaking.<br /><br />The book ended with a great twist, can't wait for The Future (#3).</span>
  <a data-text-id="4312106466170458976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText7286806583740680273" style="display:none">In this sequel to the VanWest past, Kenneth Thomas phenomenally proves that he has plenty of surprises left up his sleeve to muse his readers. The story works perfectly with a strong ending that goes so well with the different strands of the journey that took place in the preceding title. The author ends this mysteriously engorging tale with a coherent and powerful finale. Overall VanWest series is a complete mystery package for readers who enjoy fiction with a twist of love, dark secrets, power lust, and evil enemy.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15389420388794330168">Thomas strikes again with 'The Present', the second instalment of the VanWest series. Without any spoilers, the second part of the VanWest's journey picks up the action right where the first part left off. The new book answers every question that had been left hanging in mid-air in the first book. The quick-paced writing and action that made me fall in love with the first book makes a fabulous comeback. VanWest's journey across time and space is nail-biting experience, set in a world far away th</span>
  <span id="freeText15389420388794330168" style="display:none">Thomas strikes again with 'The Present', the second instalment of the VanWest series. Without any spoilers, the second part of the VanWest's journey picks up the action right where the first part left off. The new book answers every question that had been left hanging in mid-air in the first book. The quick-paced writing and action that made me fall in love with the first book makes a fabulous comeback. VanWest's journey across time and space is nail-biting experience, set in a world far away that feels so realistic and true to life nonetheless. If you liked 'The Past', you're gonna love 'The Present'. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6997348572540793657">This is a refreshing sci-fi novel that really has twists, turns, and action at every corner. I couldn't put the book down after I started reading it!   <span id="freeText6997348572540793657" style="display:none">This is a refreshing sci-fi novel that really has twists, turns, and action at every corner. I couldn't put the book down after I started reading it! I was impressed at how high-octane this book was, and how it had a lot of the same energy as the first book. It does take place right after the first book, so the whole book definitely has a really good vibe to it. <br />Amazing characters, fun story, and truly something that sci-fi fans will enjoy. Many people who read these books look for a good story, and this one has it. I definitely recommend this if you're someone who likes sci-fi books with a great, engaging plot to them. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ufmut5hwXq25fpZcRu82tL4fr0EjznA80zkGf38UFx1r38dlIy6XxR5VIj2xGjxraEBIie1D/luIR0DOslflhw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('z7H8R43oFlAsxl+HwUetz9aPzQQ20M5egMn3mjsh7Nz1l5WVNrbfOIvt6+Y2sqcQANAqzPhdQDnbt7Er9mIeRg==')})
  }
//]]>
